					<div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" lang="en" dir="ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Town in Uttar Pradesh, India</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about the municipality in Uttar Pradesh, India. For its namesake district, see <a href="/wiki/Mathura_district" title="Mathura district">Mathura district</a>.</div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Mathura_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Mathura (disambiguation)">Mathura (disambiguation)</a>.</div>

<p><b>Mathura</b> (<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Mathura.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a></span></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/41/Mathura.ogg" class="internal" title="Mathura.ogg">pronunciation</a></span>&#160;<small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">(<a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Media help"><span style="cursor:help;">help</span></a>·<a href="/wiki/File:Mathura.ogg" title="File:Mathura.ogg"><span style="cursor:help;">info</span></a>)</small></span>) is a city and the administrative headquarters of <a href="/wiki/Mathura_district" title="Mathura district">Mathura district</a> in the <a href="/wiki/States_and_union_territories_of_India" title="States and union territories of India">Indian state</a> of <a href="/wiki/Uttar_Pradesh" title="Uttar Pradesh">Uttar Pradesh</a>. It is located approximately 57.6 kilometres (35.8&#160;mi) north of <a href="/wiki/Agra" title="Agra">Agra</a>, and 146 kilometres (91&#160;mi) south-east of <a href="/wiki/Delhi" title="Delhi">Delhi</a>; about 14.5 kilometres (9.0&#160;mi) from the town of <a href="/wiki/Vrindavan" title="Vrindavan">Vrindavan</a>, and 22 kilometres (14&#160;mi) from <a href="/wiki/Govardhan" title="Govardhan">Govardhan</a>. In ancient times, Mathura was an <a href="/wiki/Economic" class="mw-redirect" title="Economic">economic</a> hub, located at the junction of important <a href="/wiki/Caravan_(travellers)" title="Caravan (travellers)">caravan</a> routes. The <a href="/wiki/2011_Census_of_India" title="2011 Census of India">2011 Census of India</a> estimated the population of Mathura at 441,894.
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a>, Mathura is the birthplace of <a href="/wiki/Krishna" title="Krishna">Krishna</a>, which is located at the <a href="/wiki/Krishna_Janmasthan_Temple_Complex" title="Krishna Janmasthan Temple Complex">Krishna Janmasthan Temple Complex</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Prasad_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Prasad-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> It is one of the <a href="/wiki/Sapta_Puri" title="Sapta Puri">Sapta Puri</a>, the seven cities considered holy by <a href="/wiki/Hindus" title="Hindus">Hindus</a>, also is called Mokshyadayni Tirth. The <a href="/wiki/Kesava_Deo_Temple" class="mw-redirect" title="Kesava Deo Temple">Kesava Deo Temple</a> was built in ancient times on the site of Krishna's birthplace (an underground <a href="/wiki/Prison" title="Prison">prison</a>). Mathura was the capital of the kingdom of <a href="/wiki/Surasena" title="Surasena">Surasena</a>, ruled by <a href="/wiki/Kamsa" title="Kamsa">Kamsa</a>, the maternal uncle of Krishna. Mathura is part of the <a href="/wiki/Krishna" title="Krishna">Krishna</a> circuit (Mathura, Vrindavan, <a href="/wiki/Barsana" title="Barsana">Barsana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Govardhan" title="Govardhan">Govardhan</a>, <a href="/wiki/48_kos_parikrama_of_Kurukshetra" class="mw-redirect" title="48 kos parikrama of Kurukshetra">Kurukshetra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dwarka" title="Dwarka">Dwarka</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bhalka" title="Bhalka">Bhalka</a>). <a href="/wiki/Janmashtami" class="mw-redirect" title="Janmashtami">Janmashtami</a> is grandly celebrated in Mathura every year.
</p><p>Mathura has been chosen as one of the heritage cities for the <a href="/wiki/Heritage_City_Development_and_Augmentation_Yojana" title="Heritage City Development and Augmentation Yojana">Heritage City Development and Augmentation Yojana</a> scheme of Government of India.<sup id="cite_ref-holycity_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-holycity-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mathura&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2><p>
Traditionally it is believed that it was founded by <a href="/wiki/Shatrughna" title="Shatrughna">Shatrughna</a> after killing <a href="/wiki/Yadava" title="Yadava">Yadava</a> <a href="/wiki/Lavana" title="Lavana">Lavana</a> at the site of Madhuvana. According to <a href="/wiki/Ramayana" title="Ramayana">Ramayana</a> it was founded by <a href="/wiki/Madhu" title="Madhu">Madhu</a> (a man of the <a href="/wiki/Yadu" class="mw-redirect" title="Yadu">Yadu tribe</a>). Later on Madhu's son <a href="/wiki/Lavanasura" title="Lavanasura">Lavanasura</a> was defeated by Satrughana.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Madhu says all the territory of Mathura belongs to <a href="/wiki/Abhiras" class="mw-redirect" title="Abhiras">Abhiras</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"></p><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Mathura_art" class="mw-redirect" title="Mathura art">Mathura art</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Edwin_Lord_Weeks_-_Along_the_Ghats,_Mathura.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Edwin_Lord_Weeks_-_Along_the_Ghats%2C_Mathura.jpg/220px-Edwin_Lord_Weeks_-_Along_the_Ghats%2C_Mathura.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="161" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Edwin_Lord_Weeks_-_Along_the_Ghats%2C_Mathura.jpg/330px-Edwin_Lord_Weeks_-_Along_the_Ghats%2C_Mathura.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Edwin_Lord_Weeks_-_Along_the_Ghats%2C_Mathura.jpg/440px-Edwin_Lord_Weeks_-_Along_the_Ghats%2C_Mathura.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5443" data-file-height="3990" /></a><figcaption>Along the Ghats of Mathura (<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">&#8201;1880</span>)</figcaption></figure>

<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:*Bindrabun_-Vrindavan-._Gate_of_Shet_Lukhmeechund%27s_Temple;_a_photo_by_Eugene_Clutterbuck_Impey,_1860%27s.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/%2ABindrabun_-Vrindavan-._Gate_of_Shet_Lukhmeechund%27s_Temple%3B_a_photo_by_Eugene_Clutterbuck_Impey%2C_1860%27s.jpg/170px-%2ABindrabun_-Vrindavan-._Gate_of_Shet_Lukhmeechund%27s_Temple%3B_a_photo_by_Eugene_Clutterbuck_Impey%2C_1860%27s.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="204" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/%2ABindrabun_-Vrindavan-._Gate_of_Shet_Lukhmeechund%27s_Temple%3B_a_photo_by_Eugene_Clutterbuck_Impey%2C_1860%27s.jpg/255px-%2ABindrabun_-Vrindavan-._Gate_of_Shet_Lukhmeechund%27s_Temple%3B_a_photo_by_Eugene_Clutterbuck_Impey%2C_1860%27s.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/%2ABindrabun_-Vrindavan-._Gate_of_Shet_Lukhmeechund%27s_Temple%3B_a_photo_by_Eugene_Clutterbuck_Impey%2C_1860%27s.jpg/340px-%2ABindrabun_-Vrindavan-._Gate_of_Shet_Lukhmeechund%27s_Temple%3B_a_photo_by_Eugene_Clutterbuck_Impey%2C_1860%27s.jpg 2x" data-file-width="712" data-file-height="854" /></a><figcaption>Gate of Shet Lukhmeechund's Temple, a photo by Eugene Clutterbuck Impey, 1860s.</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Kanishka_enhanced.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Kanishka_enhanced.jpg/170px-Kanishka_enhanced.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="276" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Kanishka_enhanced.jpg/255px-Kanishka_enhanced.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Kanishka_enhanced.jpg/340px-Kanishka_enhanced.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3053" data-file-height="4954" /></a><figcaption>Statue of <a href="/wiki/Kanishka_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Kanishka I">Kanishka I</a>, second century CE, <a href="/wiki/Mathura_Museum" class="mw-redirect" title="Mathura Museum">Mathura Museum</a>.</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:KITLV_87971_-_Unknown_-_Sculpture_of_a_woman_at_Mathura_in_British_India_-_1897.tif" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/KITLV_87971_-_Unknown_-_Sculpture_of_a_woman_at_Mathura_in_British_India_-_1897.tif/lossy-page1-170px-KITLV_87971_-_Unknown_-_Sculpture_of_a_woman_at_Mathura_in_British_India_-_1897.tif.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="345" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/KITLV_87971_-_Unknown_-_Sculpture_of_a_woman_at_Mathura_in_British_India_-_1897.tif/lossy-page1-255px-KITLV_87971_-_Unknown_-_Sculpture_of_a_woman_at_Mathura_in_British_India_-_1897.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/KITLV_87971_-_Unknown_-_Sculpture_of_a_woman_at_Mathura_in_British_India_-_1897.tif/lossy-page1-340px-KITLV_87971_-_Unknown_-_Sculpture_of_a_woman_at_Mathura_in_British_India_-_1897.tif.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2664" data-file-height="5403" /></a><figcaption>Sculpture of woman from ancient Braj-Mathura ca. second century CE.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Mathura, which lies at the centre of the cultural region of <a href="/wiki/Braj" title="Braj">Braj</a><sup id="cite_ref-LuciaMichelutti1_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LuciaMichelutti1-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> has an ancient history and is also believed to be the homeland and birthplace of Krishna, who belonged to the <a href="/wiki/Yadu" class="mw-redirect" title="Yadu">Yadu</a> dynasty. According to the <a href="/wiki/Archaeological_Survey_of_India" title="Archaeological Survey of India">Archaeological Survey of India</a> plaque at the <a href="/wiki/Mathura_Museum" class="mw-redirect" title="Mathura Museum">Mathura Museum</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Britishlibrary_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britishlibrary-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> the city is mentioned in the oldest Indian epic, the <i>Ramayana</i>. In the epic, the <a href="/wiki/Ikshwaku" class="mw-redirect" title="Ikshwaku">Ikshwaku</a> prince Shatrughna slays a demon called Lavanasura and claims the land. Afterwards, the place came to be known as <a href="/wiki/Madhuvan" class="mw-redirect" title="Madhuvan">Madhuvan</a> as it was thickly wooded, then Madhupura and later Mathura.<sup id="cite_ref-p1_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p1-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The most important pilgrimage site in Mathura was Katra ('market place'), now referred to as <a href="/wiki/Krishna" title="Krishna">Krishna</a> Janmasthan ('the birthplace of Krishna'). Excavations at the site revealed pottery and terracotta dating to the sixth century BCE, the remains of a large <a href="/wiki/Buddhist" class="mw-redirect" title="Buddhist">Buddhist</a> complex, including a monastery called Yasha Vihara of the <a href="/wiki/Gupta_Empire" title="Gupta Empire">Gupta</a> period, as well as <a href="/wiki/Jainism" title="Jainism">Jain</a> sculptures of the same era.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancient_history">Ancient history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mathura&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Ancient history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Archaeological excavations at Mathura show the gradual growth of a village into an important city during the <a href="/wiki/Vedic_age" class="mw-redirect" title="Vedic age">Vedic age</a>. The earliest period belonged to the <a href="/wiki/Painted_Grey_Ware_culture" title="Painted Grey Ware culture">Painted Grey Ware culture</a> (1100–500 BCE), followed by the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Black_Polished_Ware" title="Northern Black Polished Ware">Northern Black Polished Ware</a> culture (700–200 BCE). Mathura derived its importance as a center of trade due to its location where the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Trunk_Road" title="Grand Trunk Road">northern trade route</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Indo-Gangetic_Plain" title="Indo-Gangetic Plain">Indo-Gangetic Plain</a> met with the routes to <a href="/wiki/Malwa" title="Malwa">Malwa</a> (central India) and the <a href="/wiki/Western_India" title="Western India">west coast</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Singh2008_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Singh2008-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Archaeologists have discovered a fragment of Mathura red sandstone from <a href="/wiki/Rakhigarhi" title="Rakhigarhi">Rakhigarhi</a> - a site of <a href="/wiki/Indus_Valley_civilisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Indus Valley civilisation">Indus Valley civilization</a> dated to third millennium BCE - which was used as a grindstone; red sandstone was also a popular material for <a href="/wiki/Art_of_Mathura" title="Art of Mathura">historic period sculptures</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>By the sixth century BCE Mathura became the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Surasena" title="Surasena">Surasena Kingdom</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ImpGazetteer_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ImpGazetteer-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The city was later ruled by the <a href="/wiki/Maurya" class="mw-redirect" title="Maurya">Maurya</a> empire (fourth to second centuries BCE). <a href="/wiki/Megasthenes" title="Megasthenes">Megasthenes</a>, writing in the early third century BCE, mentions Mathura as a great city under the name Μέθορα (<i>Méthora</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> It seems it never was under the direct control of the following <a href="/wiki/Shunga_Empire" title="Shunga Empire">Shunga</a> dynasty (2nd century BCE) as not a single archaeological remain of a Shunga presence were ever found in Mathura.<sup id="cite_ref-Rhie_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rhie-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Indo-Greeks" class="mw-redirect" title="Indo-Greeks">Indo-Greeks</a> may have taken control, direct or indirect, of Mathura some time between 180 BCE and 100 BCE, and remained so as late as 70 BCE according to the <a href="/wiki/Yavanarajya_inscription" title="Yavanarajya inscription">Yavanarajya inscription</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Rhie_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rhie-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> which was found in <a href="/wiki/Maghera" title="Maghera">Maghera</a>, a town 17 kilometres (11&#160;mi) from Mathura.<sup id="cite_ref-BotAI_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BotAI-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The opening of the 3 line text of this inscription in <a href="/wiki/Brahmi_script" title="Brahmi script">Brahmi script</a> translates as: "In the 116th year of the <a href="/wiki/Yavana" class="mw-redirect" title="Yavana">Yavana</a> kingdom..."<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> or '"In the 116th year of Yavana hegemony" ("<i>Yavanarajya</i>")<sup id="cite_ref-Rhie_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rhie-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> However, this also corresponds to the presence of the native <a href="/wiki/Mitra_dynasty_(Mathura)" title="Mitra dynasty (Mathura)">Mitra dynasty</a> of local rulers in Mathura, in approximately the same time frame (150 BCE—50 BCE), possibly pointing to a vassalage relationship with the Indo-Greeks.<sup id="cite_ref-Rhie_19-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rhie-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Indo-Scythians">Indo-Scythians</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mathura&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Indo-Scythians">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>After a period of local rule, Mathura was conquered by the <a href="/wiki/Indo-Scythians" title="Indo-Scythians">Indo-Scythians</a> during the first century BCE. The Indo-Scythian satraps of Mathura are sometimes called the "<a href="/wiki/Northern_Satraps" title="Northern Satraps">Northern Satraps</a>", as opposed to the "<a href="/wiki/Western_Satraps" title="Western Satraps">Western Satraps</a>" ruling in <a href="/wiki/Gujarat" title="Gujarat">Gujarat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malwa" title="Malwa">Malwa</a>. However, Indo-Scythian control proved to be short lived, following the reign of the Indo-Scythian <i>Mahakshatrapa</i> ("Great Satrap") <a href="/wiki/Rajuvula" title="Rajuvula">Rajuvula</a>, <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">&#8201;10</span>–25 CE. The Mora Well inscription of Mahakshatrapa <a href="/wiki/Rajuvula" title="Rajuvula">Rajuvula</a>, of the early decades of the first century CE, found in a village seven miles from Mathura, stated that images <i>pratima(h)</i> of the blessed (<i>bhagavatam</i>) five <a href="/wiki/Vrishni_heroes" title="Vrishni heroes">Vrishni heroes</a>, were installed in a stone shrine of a person called Tosa.<sup id="cite_ref-auto2_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> The heroes were identified from a passage in the <a href="/wiki/Vayu_Purana" title="Vayu Purana">Vayu Purana</a> as Samkarsana, <a href="/wiki/Vasudeva" title="Vasudeva">Vasudev</a>, Pradyumna, Samba, and Aniruddha.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The English translation of the inscription read:-
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>. . . of the son of mahakṣatrapa Rāṃjūvula, svāmi . . . The images of the holy paṃcavīras of the Vṛṣṇis is... the stone shrine... whom the magnificent matchless stone house of Toṣā was erected and maintained... five objects of adoration made of stone, radiant, as it were with highest beauty...<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>The Mathura inscription of the time of Mahakshatrapa <a href="/wiki/Rajuvula" title="Rajuvula">Rajuvula</a>'s son, Mahakshatrapa <a href="/wiki/Sodasa" title="Sodasa">Sodasa</a> recorded erection of a <i>torana</i> (gateway), <i>vedika</i> (terrace) and <i>chatuhsala</i> (quadrangle) at the <i>Mahasthana</i> (great place) of Bhagavat Vasudeva.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Several male torsos representing the Vrisni heroes were also found in a shrine in Mora dating to the time of Mahakshatrapa <a href="/wiki/Sodasa" title="Sodasa">Sodasa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-auto2_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Kushan_Empire">Kushan Empire</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mathura&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Kushan Empire">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>During the rule of the great <a href="/wiki/Kushan" class="mw-redirect" title="Kushan">Kushanas</a>, art and culture flourished in the region and reached new heights and is now famously known as the <a href="/wiki/Art_of_Mathura" title="Art of Mathura">Mathura School of Art</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Kushan" class="mw-redirect" title="Kushan">Kushans</a> took control of Mathura some time after Mahakshatrapa <a href="/wiki/Sodasa" title="Sodasa">Sodasa</a>, although several of his successors ruled as Kushans vassals, such as the Indo-Scythian "Great Satrap" <a href="/wiki/Kharapallana" title="Kharapallana">Kharapallana</a> and the "Satrap" <a href="/wiki/Vanaspara" title="Vanaspara">Vanaspara</a>, both of whom paid allegiance to the Kushans in an inscription at <a href="/wiki/Sarnath" title="Sarnath">Sarnath</a>, dating to the third year of the reign of the Kushan emperor <a href="/wiki/Kanishka" title="Kanishka">Kanishka the Great</a> <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">&#8201;130</span> CE.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Mathuran art and culture reached its zenith under the <a href="/wiki/Kushan" class="mw-redirect" title="Kushan">Kushan</a> dynasty which had Mathura as one of its capitals.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> The preceding capitals of the Kushans included <a href="/wiki/Kapisa_(city)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kapisa (city)">Kapisa</a> (modern Bagram, Afghanistan), <a href="/wiki/Purushapura" class="mw-redirect" title="Purushapura">Purushapura</a> (modern Peshawar, Pakistan) and <a href="/wiki/Taxila" title="Taxila">Takshasila</a>/<a href="/wiki/Sirsukh" title="Sirsukh">Sirsukh</a>/ (modern Taxila, Pakistan). Mathura ateliers were most active during the epoch of the great <a href="/wiki/Kushan" class="mw-redirect" title="Kushan">Kushan</a> emperors <a href="/wiki/Kanishka" title="Kanishka">Kanishka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Huvishka" title="Huvishka">Huvishka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vasudeva_I" title="Vasudeva I">Vasudeva</a> whose reign represents the Golden Age of Mathura <a href="/wiki/Sculpture" title="Sculpture">sculpture</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> During the third century, <a href="/wiki/Nagas_of_Padmavati" title="Nagas of Padmavati">Nagas</a> ruled Mathura after decline of Kushan Empire.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAshvini_Agrawal198954_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAshvini_Agrawal198954-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Gupta_Empire">Gupta Empire</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mathura&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Gupta Empire">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In the reign of <a href="/wiki/Chandragupta_Vikramaditya" class="mw-redirect" title="Chandragupta Vikramaditya">Chandragupta Vikramaditya</a>, a magnificent temple of <a href="/wiki/Vishnu" title="Vishnu">Vishnu</a> was built at the site of Katra Keshavadeva.<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kalidasa" title="Kalidasa">Kalidasa</a>, hailed as the greatest poet and dramatist in <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a>, in the fourth-fifth century CE mentioned the groves of <a href="/wiki/Vrindavan" title="Vrindavan">Vrindavan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Govardhan" title="Govardhan">Govardhan</a> hill as:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942"><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>"...the king of Mathura, whose fame was acknowledged in song even by the devatas... At that moment, though still in Mathura, it appears as if Ganga has merged with Yamuna at the Sangam... In a Vrindavan garden which is superior even to Kubera's garden, known as Chaitra-ratha... You can, as well, during rains, look at the dancing peacocks, while sitting in a pleasant cave of the Goverdhan Mountain"<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>Chinese Buddhist Monk <a href="/wiki/Faxian" title="Faxian">Faxian</a> mentions the city as a centre of Buddhism about 400 CE. He found the people were very well off, there were no taxes other than for those on farmers who tilled the royal land. He found that people did not kill animals, no one consumed wine, and did not eat onion or garlic.  He found that engraved title deeds were issued to land owners. Visiting priests were provided with accommodation, beds, mats, food, drinks and clothes to perform scholarly works.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (March 2020)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Harsha_Empire">Harsha Empire</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mathura&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Harsha Empire">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Xuanzang" title="Xuanzang">Xuanzang</a>, who visited the city in 634 CE, mentions it as Mot'ulo, recording that it contained twenty Buddhist monasteries and many Hindu temples.<sup id="cite_ref-rongxi103_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rongxi103-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EB1911_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB1911-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Later, he went east to <a href="/wiki/Thanesar" title="Thanesar">Thanesar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jalandhar" title="Jalandhar">Jalandhar</a> in the eastern <a href="/wiki/Punjab_region" class="mw-redirect" title="Punjab region">Punjab</a>, before climbing up to visit predominantly <a href="/wiki/Theravada" title="Theravada">Theravada</a> monasteries in the <a href="/wiki/Kulu_valley" class="mw-redirect" title="Kulu valley">Kulu valley</a> and turning southward again to <a href="/wiki/Bairat" class="mw-redirect" title="Bairat">Bairat</a> and then Mathura, on the <a href="/wiki/Yamuna_river" class="mw-redirect" title="Yamuna river">Yamuna river</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medieval_History_and_Islamic_Invasions">Medieval History and Islamic Invasions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mathura&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Medieval History and Islamic Invasions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_Middle_Ages">Early Middle Ages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mathura&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Early Middle Ages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The famous female <a href="/wiki/Alvars" title="Alvars">Alvar</a> saint, <a href="/wiki/Andal" title="Andal">Andal</a> visualized going to a pilgrimage which began at Mathura, then proceeded to <a href="/wiki/Gokul" title="Gokul">Gokul</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Yamuna" title="Yamuna">Yamuna</a>, the pool of Kaliya, <a href="/wiki/Vrindavan" title="Vrindavan">Vrindavan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Govardhan" title="Govardhan">Govardhan</a>, and finished at <a href="/wiki/Dwarka" title="Dwarka">Dwarka</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> The eleventh century Kashmiri poet, <a href="/wiki/Bilhana" title="Bilhana">Bilhana</a> visited Mathura and <a href="/wiki/Vrindavan" title="Vrindavan">Vrindavan</a> after leaving Kashmir en route to Karnataka.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="High_Middle_Ages">High Middle Ages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mathura&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: High Middle Ages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The city was sacked and many of its temples destroyed by <a href="/wiki/Mahmud_of_Ghazni" title="Mahmud of Ghazni">Mahmud of Ghazni</a> in 1018 CE.<sup id="cite_ref-EB1911_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB1911-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The capture of Mathura by <a href="/wiki/Mahmud_of_Ghazni" title="Mahmud of Ghazni">Maḥmūd Ibn Sebüktegīn</a> is described by the historian al-Utbi (Abu Nasr Muhammad ibn Muhammad al Jabbaru-l 'Utbi) in his work <a href="/wiki/Tarikh_Yamini" title="Tarikh Yamini">Tarikh Yamini</a> as follows:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942"><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>The wall of the city was constructed of hard stone, and two gates opened upon the river flowing under the city, which were erected upon strong and lofty foundations, to protect them against the floods of the river and rains. On both sides of the city there were a thousand houses, to which idol temples were attached, all strengthened from top to bottom by rivets of iron, and all made of masonry work; and opposite to them were other buildings, supported on broad wooden pillars, to give them strength.</p></blockquote>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942"><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>In the middle of the city there was a temple larger and firmer than the rest, which can neither be described nor painted. The Sultan thus wrote respecting it&#160;:— “ If any should wish to construct a building equal to this, he would not be able to do it without expending an hundred thousand thousand red dinars, and it would occupy two hundred years, even though the most experienced and able workmen were employed.” Among the idols there were five made of red gold, each five yards high, fixed in the air without support. In the eyes of one of these idols there were two rubies, of such value, that if any one were to sell such as are like them, he would obtain fifty thousand dinars. On another, there was a sapphire purer than water, and more sparkling than crystal; the weight was four hundred and fifty miskals. The two feet of another idol weighed four thousand four hundred miskals, and the entire quantity of gold yielded by the bodies of these idols, was ninety-eight thousand three hundred miskals. The idols of silver amounted to two hundred, but they could not be weighed without breaking them to pieces and putting them into scales. The Sultan gave orders that all the temples should be burnt with naphtha and fire, and levelled with the ground.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>The temple at Katra was sacked by <a href="/wiki/Mahmud_of_Ghazni" title="Mahmud of Ghazni">Maḥmūd Ibn Sebüktegīn</a>. A temple was built to replace it in 1150 CE. The Mathura <i>prasasti</i> (Eulogistic Inscription) dated <a href="/wiki/Vikram_Samvat" title="Vikram Samvat">Samvat (V.S.)</a> 1207 (1150 CE), said to have been found in 1889 CE at the Keshava mound by <a href="/wiki/Alois_Anton_F%C3%BChrer" title="Alois Anton Führer">Anton Fuhrer</a>, German Indologist who worked with the Archaeological Survey of India, recorded the foundations of a temple dedicated to <a href="/wiki/Vishnu" title="Vishnu">Vishnu</a> at the Katra site:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942"><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Jajja, who carried the burden of the varga, together with a committee of trustees (goshtijana), built a large temple of Vishnu, brilliantly white and touching the clouds.</p></blockquote>
<p>Jajja was a vassal of the <a href="/wiki/Gahadavala_dynasty" title="Gahadavala dynasty">Gahadavalas</a> in charge of Mathura, and the committee mentioned in the <i>prasasti</i> could have been of an earlier <a href="/wiki/Vaishnavism" title="Vaishnavism">Vaishnava</a> temple.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> The temple built by Jajja at Katra was destroyed by the forces of <a href="/wiki/Qutb_al-Din_Aibak" class="mw-redirect" title="Qutb al-Din Aibak">Qutubuddin Aibak</a>, though <a href="/wiki/Firuz_Shah_Tughlaq" title="Firuz Shah Tughlaq">Feroz Tughlaq</a> (r. 1351–88 CE) was also said to have attacked it.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> It was repaired and survived till the reign of <a href="/wiki/Sikandar_Lodi" class="mw-redirect" title="Sikandar Lodi">Sikandar Lodi</a> (r. 1489–1517 CE).
</p><p>In the twelfth century, Bhatta Lakshmidhara, chief minister of the <a href="/wiki/Gahadavala_dynasty" title="Gahadavala dynasty">Gahadavala</a> king <a href="/wiki/Govindachandra_(Gahadavala_dynasty)" title="Govindachandra (Gahadavala dynasty)">Govindachandra</a> (r. 1114–1155 CE), wrote the earliest surviving collection of verses in praise of the sacred sites of Mathura in his work Krtyakalpataru, which has been described as "the first re-statement of the theory of <i>Tirtha-yatra</i> (pilgrimage)".<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> In his Krtyakalpataru, Bhatta Lakshmidhara devoted an entire section (9) to Mathura.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Later on the city was sacked again by <a href="/wiki/Sikandar_Lodi" class="mw-redirect" title="Sikandar Lodi">Sikandar Lodi</a>, who ruled the <a href="/wiki/Sultanate_of_Delhi" class="mw-redirect" title="Sultanate of Delhi">Sultanate of Delhi</a> from 1489 to 1517 CE.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sikandar_Lodi" class="mw-redirect" title="Sikandar Lodi">Sikandar Lodi</a> earned the epithet of 'Butt Shikan', the 'Destroyer of Idols'. <a href="/wiki/Firishta" title="Firishta">Ferishta</a> recorded that <a href="/wiki/Sikandar_Lodi" class="mw-redirect" title="Sikandar Lodi">Sikandar Lodi</a> was a staunch Muslim, with a passion for vandalizing heathen temples:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942"><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>He was firmly attached to the Mahomedan religion, and made a point of destroying all Hindu temples. In the city of Mathura he caused masjids and bazaars to be built opposite the bathing-stairs leading to the river, and ordered that no Hindus should be allowed to bathe there. He forbade the barbers to shave the beards and heads of the inhabitants, in order to prevent the Hindus following their usual practices at such pilgrimages.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>In Tarikh-i Daudi, of 'Abdu-lla (written during the time of <a href="/wiki/Jahangir" title="Jahangir">Jahangir</a>) said of <a href="/wiki/Sikandar_Lodi" class="mw-redirect" title="Sikandar Lodi">Sikandar Lodi</a>:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942"><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>He was so zealous a Musulman that he utterly destroyed divers places of worship of the infidels, and left not a vestige remaining of them. He entirely ruined the shrines of Mathura, the mine of heathenism, and turned their principal Hindu places of worship into caravanserais and colleges. Their stone images were given to the butchers to serve them as meat-weights, and all the Hindus in Mathura were strictly prohibited from shaving their heads and beards, and performing their ablutions. He thus put an end to all the idolatrous rites of the infidels there; and no Hindu, if he wished to have his head or beard shaved, could get a barber to do it. Every city thus conformed as he desired to the customs of Islam.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p><a href="/wiki/Vallabha" title="Vallabha">Vallabhacharya</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chaitanya_Mahaprabhu" title="Chaitanya Mahaprabhu">Chaitanya Mahaprabhu</a> arrived in the Braj region, in search of sacred places that had been destroyed or lost. In <i>Shrikrsnashrayah</i>, that make up the <i>Sodashagrantha</i>, <a href="/wiki/Vallabha" title="Vallabha">Vallabha</a> said of his age:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942"><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>The Malechchhas (non-Hindus in this context) have surrounded all the holy places with the result that they have become infected with evil. Besides, the holy people are full of sorrow. At such a time <a href="/wiki/Krishna" title="Krishna">Krishna</a> alone is my way.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Late_Middle_Ages">Late Middle Ages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mathura&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Late Middle Ages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese</a>, Father Antonio Monserrate (1536 CE-1600 CE), who was on a Jesuit mission at the Mughal Court during the times of <a href="/wiki/Akbar" title="Akbar">Akbar</a>, visited Mathura in 1580–82, and noted that all temples built at sites associated with the deeds of <a href="/wiki/Krishna" title="Krishna">Krishna</a> were in ruins:-
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942"><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>It (Mathura) used to be a great and well populated city, with splendid buildings and a great circuit of walls. The ruins plainly indicate how imposing its buildings were. For out of these forgotten ruins are dug up columns and very ancient statues, of skilful and cunning workmanship. Only one Hindu temple is left out of many; for the Musalmans have completely destroyed all except the pyramids. Huge crowds of pilgrims come from all over India to this temple, which is situated on the high bank of the Jomanis (<a href="/wiki/Yamuna" title="Yamuna">Yamuna</a>)...<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Krishna_Janmasthan_Temple_Complex" title="Krishna Janmasthan Temple Complex">Keshavadeva temple</a> was rebuilt by the <a href="/wiki/Bundela" title="Bundela">Bundela</a> Rajput Rajah <a href="/wiki/Vir_Singh_Deo" title="Vir Singh Deo">Vir Singh Deo</a> at a cost of thirty-three lakh rupees when the gold was priced at around ₹ 10/- per <a href="/wiki/Tola_(unit)" title="Tola (unit)"><i>tola</i></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> And the grand structure of the temple in Mathura was regarded a "wonder of the age".<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Mughal_Empire" title="Mughal Empire">Mughal</a> <a href="/wiki/Aurangzeb" title="Aurangzeb">Emperor Aurangzeb</a>, built the Shahi-Eidgah Mosque during his rule, which is adjacent to <a href="/wiki/Shri_Krishna_Janmabhoomi" class="mw-redirect" title="Shri Krishna Janmabhoomi">Shri Krishna Janmabhoomi</a> believed to be over a <a href="/wiki/Hindu_temple" title="Hindu temple">Hindu temple</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> He also changed the city's name to Islamabad.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> In 1669, Aurangzeb issued a general order for the demolition of Hindu schools and temples, in 1670, specifically ordered the destruction of the Keshavadeva temple. Saqi Mustaid Khan recorded:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942"><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>On Thursday, 27th January/15 Ramzan (27 January 1670)... the Emperor as the promoter of justice and overthrower of mischief, as a knower of truth and destroyer of oppression as the zephyr of the garden of victory and the reviver of the faith of the Prophet, issued orders for the demolition of the temple situated in Mathura, famous as the Dehra of Kesho Rai. In a short time by the great exertions of his officers, the destruction of this strong foundation of infidelity was accomplished and on its site a lofty mosque was built by the expenditure of a large sum... Praised be the august God of the faith of Islam, that in the auspicious reign of this destroyer of infidelity and turbulence, such a wonderful and seemingly impossible work was successfully accomplished.</p></blockquote>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942"><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>On seeing this instance of the strength of the emperor's faith and the grandeur of his devotion to God, the proud Rajas were stifled, and in amazement they stood like images facing the wall. The idols, large and small, set with costly jewels, which had been set up in the temple, were brought to Agra, and buried under the step of the mosque of the Begum Shahib in order to be continuously trodden upon. The name of Mathura was changed to Islamabad.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>The Muslim conquest resulted in the destruction of all <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jainism" title="Jainism">Jain</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hindu</a> temples and monuments in and around Mathura. <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a>, already in decline, never revived, and for the next four hundred years the <a href="/wiki/Jainism" title="Jainism">Jains</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hindus" title="Hindus">Hindus</a> were unable to erect any temples that were not sooner or later demolished.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Many of the sites that had been places of religious importance were abandoned and gradually sank beneath the earth. But some of them were not forgotten, owing to the persistence of oral tradition, the refashioning of a temple into a mosque, or the presence of humble shrines, some of which housed sculptural fragments of earlier buildings. Several of them have survived as places of significance in the modern pilgrimage circuit.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>"The rebellion in Mathurá district seems to have gained ground. 'On the 14th Rajab, 1080, [28 November 1669], his Majesty left Dihlí for Akbarábád, and almost daily enjoyed the pleasures of the chase. On the 21st Rajab, whilst hunting, he received the report of a rebellion having broken out at Mauza' Rewarah, Chandarkah, and Surkhrú. Hasan 'Ali Khán was ordered to attack the rebels at night, which he did, and the firing lasted till 12 o'clock the next day. The rebels, unable longer to withstand, thinking of the honour of their families, now fought with short arms, and many imperial soldiers and companions of Hasan ’Alí were killed. Three hundred rebels were sent to perdition, and two hundred and fifty, men and women, caught. Hasan ’Alí, in the afternoon, reported personally the result of the fight, and was ordered to leave the prisoners and the cattle in charge of Sayyid Zain ul-'Abidin, the jágirdár of the place. Çaf Shikan Khán also (who after ’Abdunnabí's death had been appointed Faujdár of Mathura) waited on the emperor, and was ordered to tell off two hundred troopers to guard the fields attached to the villages, and prevent soldiers from plundering and kidnapping children. Námdár Khán, Faujdár of Murádábád, also came to pay his respects. Çafshikan Khán was removed from his office, and Hasan 'Ali Khán was appointed Faujdár of Mathura, with a command of Three Thousand and Five Hundred, 2000 troopers, and received a dress of honour, a sword, and a horse. * * * On the 18th Sha'bán [1st January, 1670), his Majesty entered Agrah. Kokilá Ját, the wicked ringleader of the rebels of District*......, who had been the cause of ’Abdunnabí's death and who had plundered Parganah Sa'dábád, was at last caught by Hasan ’Alí Khán and his zealous peshkár, Shaikh Razíuddin, and he was now sent with the Shaikh to Agrah, where by order of his Majesty he was executed. Kokila's son and daughter were given to Jawahir Khán Nazir [a eunuch]. The girl was later married to Shah Quli, the well-known Chelah; and his son, who was called Fázil, became in time so excellent a Hafiz [one who knows the Qorán by heart], that his Majesty preferred him to all others and even chaunted passages to him. Shaikh Razíuddin, who had captured Kokila, belonged to a respectable family in Bhagalpur, Bihár, and was an excellent soldier, administrator, and companion; he was at the same time so learned, that he was ordered to assist in the compilation of the Fatáwá i 'Alamgiri [the great code of Muhammadan laws]. He received a daily allowance of three rupees.'+ (Haásir i ’Alamgiri, pp. 92 to 91.) Hasan ’Alí Khán retained his office from 1080 to Sha'bán 1087 (October, 1676), when Sulțán Qulí Khán was appointed Faujdír of Mathurá.", <a href="/wiki/Asiatic_Society_of_Bengal" class="mw-redirect" title="Asiatic Society of Bengal">Asiatic Society of Bengal</a>, <i>Proceedings</i><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_Modern_History">Early Modern History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mathura&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Early Modern History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According the biographer of Raja <a href="/wiki/Jai_Singh_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Jai Singh II">Jai Singh</a>, Atmaram, when Jai Singh was campaigning against the Jat Raja <a href="/wiki/Churaman" title="Churaman">Churaman Singh</a>, he bathed at Radha <i>kund</i> on the full moon of Kartik, went to Mathura in the month of Shravan in 1724, and performed the marriage of his daughter on <a href="/wiki/Krishna_Janmashtami" title="Krishna Janmashtami"><i>Janmashtami</i></a>. He then undertook a tour of the sacred forests of <a href="/wiki/Braj" title="Braj">Braj</a>, and, on his return to Mathura, founded religious establishments and celebrated <a href="/wiki/Holi" title="Holi">Holi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Pilgrimage_by_the_Family_of_Peshwa_of_Maratha_Empire">Pilgrimage by the Family of Peshwa of Maratha Empire</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mathura&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Pilgrimage by the Family of Peshwa of Maratha Empire">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>During the period of the expansion of <a href="/wiki/Maratha_Empire" title="Maratha Empire">Maratha Empire</a>, pilgrimage to the holy places in the north became quite frequent. <a href="/wiki/Pilgrim" title="Pilgrim">Pilgrims</a> required protection on the way and took advantage of the constant movement of troops that journeyed to and back from their homeland for military purposes. That is how the practice arose of ladies accompanying military expeditions. The mother of <a href="/wiki/Peshwa" title="Peshwa">Peshwa</a> <a href="/wiki/Balaji_Baji_Rao" title="Balaji Baji Rao">Balaji Baji Rao</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kashibai" title="Kashibai">Kashitai</a> performed her famous pilgrimage for four years in the north, visiting Mathura, <a href="/wiki/Prayagraj" title="Prayagraj">Prayag</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ayodhya" title="Ayodhya">Ayodhya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Varanasi" title="Varanasi">Banaras</a>, and other holy places.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Religious_heritage">Religious heritage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mathura&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Religious heritage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Mathura_India_(2).JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Mathura_India_%282%29.JPG/220px-Mathura_India_%282%29.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Mathura_India_%282%29.JPG/330px-Mathura_India_%282%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Mathura_India_%282%29.JPG/440px-Mathura_India_%282%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="960" /></a><figcaption>Entrance to the <a href="/wiki/Shri_Krishna_Janmabhoomi" class="mw-redirect" title="Shri Krishna Janmabhoomi">Shri Krishna Janmabhoomi</a> temple complex.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Mathura is a holy city in Hinduism and is considered the heart of <a href="/wiki/Brij_Bhoomi" class="mw-redirect" title="Brij Bhoomi">Brij Bhoomi</a>, the land of Krishna.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Lucia_Michelutti00_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lucia_Michelutti00-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> The twin-city to Mathura is <a href="/wiki/Vrindavan" title="Vrindavan">Vrindavan</a>.
</p><p>There are many places of historic and religious importance in Mathura and its neighbouring towns.<sup id="cite_ref-holycity_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-holycity-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Krishna_Janmasthan_Temple_Complex" title="Krishna Janmasthan Temple Complex">Krishna Janmasthan Temple Complex</a> is an important group of temples built around what is considered to be the birthplace of <a href="/wiki/Krishna" title="Krishna">Krishna</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Avatar_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Avatar-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Vemsani_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vemsani-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> The temple complex contains Keshav Deva temple, Garbha Griha shrine, Bhagavata Bhavan and the Rangabhoomi where the final battle between Krishna and <a href="/wiki/Kans" class="mw-redirect" title="Kans">Kamsa</a> took place.<sup id="cite_ref-Janm_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Janm-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Prasad_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Prasad-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Britishlibrary_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britishlibrary-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Avatar_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Avatar-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Dwarkadheesh_temple_Mathura" class="mw-redirect" title="Dwarkadheesh temple Mathura">Dwarkadheesh Temple</a> is one of the largest temples in Mathura.<sup id="cite_ref-Prasad_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Prasad-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Vishram_Ghat" title="Vishram Ghat">Vishram Ghat</a> at the bank of river Yamuna is said to be the place were Krishna had rested after killing <a href="/wiki/Kans" class="mw-redirect" title="Kans">Kamsa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Prasad_7-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Prasad-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Other notable Hindu religious sites and heritage locations includes the Gita Mandir,<sup id="cite_ref-Mathura1_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mathura1-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> Govind Dev temple,<sup id="cite_ref-Mathura1_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mathura1-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/ISKCON" class="mw-redirect" title="ISKCON">ISKCON</a> temple,<sup id="cite_ref-Prasad_7-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Prasad-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kusum_Sarovar" title="Kusum Sarovar">Kusum Sarovar</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Mathura1_63-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mathura1-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Naam_yog_Sadhna_Mandir" title="Naam yog Sadhna Mandir">Naam yog Sadhna Mandir</a>, Peepleshwar Mahadeo Temple<sup id="cite_ref-MathuraTT_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MathuraTT-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> and Yum Yamuna Temple<sup id="cite_ref-MathuraTT_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MathuraTT-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Kankali_Tila" title="Kankali Tila">Kankali Tila</a> brought forth many treasures of Jain art. The archaeological findings testify the existence of two Jain temples and stupas. Numerous Jain sculptures, <a href="/wiki/Ayagapata" title="Ayagapata">Ayagapatas</a> (tablet of homage),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDas1980171_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDas1980171-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> pillars, crossbeams and lintels were found during archaeological excavations.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVyas199516_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVyas199516-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> Some of the sculptures are provided with inscriptions that report on the contemporary society and organization of the Jain community.
</p><p>Most sculptures could be dated from the second century BC to the 12th century CE, thus representing a continuous period of about 14 centuries during which <a href="/wiki/Jainism" title="Jainism">Jainism</a> flourished at Mathura.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVyas199516_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVyas199516-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> These sculptures are now housed in the Lucknow State Museum and in the Mathura Museum.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Mathura_Museum" class="mw-redirect" title="Mathura Museum">Mathura Museum</a> is notable for archaeological artefacts, especially those from the <a href="/wiki/Kushan_Empire" title="Kushan Empire">Kushan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gupta_Empire" title="Gupta Empire">Gupta</a> empires. It has sculptures associated with Hinduism, Buddhism and Jainism.<sup id="cite_ref-Britishlibrary_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britishlibrary-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Festivals">Festivals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mathura&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Festivals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Krishna_Janmashtami" title="Krishna Janmashtami">Krishna Janmashtami</a></div>
<p>Krishna Janmashtami is grandly celebrated every year in Mathura. Every year 3 to 3.5&#160;million devotees celebrate Janmashtami in Mathura, with the maximum number of devotees visiting the Keshav Deva temple and the Dwarkadheesh temple.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Devotees generally observe a fast and break it at midnight when Krishna was believed to have been born. Devotional songs, dance performances, <a href="/wiki/Bhog" title="Bhog">bhog</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aarti" class="mw-redirect" title="Aarti">aartis</a> are observed across Mathura-Vrindavan.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mathura&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Mathura is located at <span class="geo-inline"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1156832818"><span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="https://geohack.toolforge.org/geohack.php?pagename=Mathura&amp;params=27.28_N_77.41_E_"><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">27°17′N</span> <span class="longitude">77°25′E</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">27.28°N 77.41°E</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">27.28; 77.41</span></span></span></a></span></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> It has an average elevation of 174&#160;metres (570&#160;<a href="/wiki/Foot_(length)" class="mw-redirect" title="Foot (length)">feet</a>).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mathura&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mathura&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;">

<p>The <a href="/wiki/2011_census_of_India" class="mw-redirect" title="2011 census of India">2011 census of India</a> estimates the population of Mathura to be 441,894, with a decadal growth rate of 22.53 per cent. Males account for 54% (268,445) and females for 46% (173,449) of this population. Sex ratio of Mathura is 858 females per 1000 males, which has increased from 840 (2001). However, national sex ratio is 940. Population density in 2011 has increased from 621 per km<sup>2</sup> in 2001 to 761 per km<sup>2</sup>. Mathura has an average literacy rate of 72.65 per cent which has increased from 61.46 percent (2001) but still lower than the national average of 74.04 per cent. Male and female literacy rate are 84.39 and 58.93 per cent respectively. 15.61 percent of Mathura's population is under 6 years of age. This figure was 19.56 per cent in 2001 census.<sup id="cite_ref-census2011_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census2011-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mathura&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to the 2011 census on Mathura NPP, 95.4% of the people identified as <a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">Hindi</a> speakers, 2.6% as <a href="/wiki/Urdu" title="Urdu">Urdu</a> speakers and 1.4% as speakers of <a href="/wiki/Braj_Bhasha" title="Braj Bhasha">Braj Bhasha</a><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> (the local dialect).<sup id="cite_ref-LuciaMichelutti1_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LuciaMichelutti1-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The city also lies within the cultural region of <a href="/wiki/Braj" title="Braj">Braj</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LuciaMichelutti1_6-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LuciaMichelutti1-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mathura&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Actress turned political leader, <a href="/wiki/Hema_Malini" title="Hema Malini">Hema Malini</a> is the sitting MP of holy constituency Mathura in Uttar Pradesh.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mathura&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mathura&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:MTJ_-_Mathura_Junction_Railway_Station.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/MTJ_-_Mathura_Junction_Railway_Station.jpg/220px-MTJ_-_Mathura_Junction_Railway_Station.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/MTJ_-_Mathura_Junction_Railway_Station.jpg/330px-MTJ_-_Mathura_Junction_Railway_Station.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/MTJ_-_Mathura_Junction_Railway_Station.jpg/440px-MTJ_-_Mathura_Junction_Railway_Station.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2851" data-file-height="1900" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Mathura_Junction_railway_station" title="Mathura Junction railway station">Mathura Junction railway station</a> lies on the Delhi-Mumbai rail route.</figcaption></figure>
<p><a href="/wiki/Mathura_Junction_railway_station" title="Mathura Junction railway station">Mathura Junction railway station</a> is situated on the major Delhi-Mumbai rail route. Both Central Railway and Western Railway routes pass through Mathura. Trains from NCR (north-central railway) to ER (eastern railway) also pass through the Mathura junction. <a href="/wiki/Mathura_Cantt_railway_station" title="Mathura Cantt railway station">Mathura Cantt railway station</a> is a major route for eastern and central railway.
</p><p>Important trains that originate/terminate at Mathura are:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Chambal_Express" title="Chambal Express">12177/Howrah – Mathura Chambal Express</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Road">Road</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mathura&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Road">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Mathura is well-connected by road to the rest of India. <a href="/wiki/National_highways_of_India" title="National highways of India">National Highway</a> NH-19(previously <a href="/wiki/National_Highway_2_(India)" title="National Highway 2 (India)">NH-2</a>) from Delhi to Kolkata, with diversion for Chennai also passes through Mathura. <a href="/wiki/Yamuna_Expressway" title="Yamuna Expressway">Yamuna Expressway</a> from Greater-Noida to Agra (165&#160;km 6 lane access controlled express highway) also passes through, providing good connectivity to Noida, Agra, Kanpur and Lucknow.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tram">Tram</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mathura&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Tram">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Tram" title="Tram">tram</a> network has been proposed in the city, which would make Mathura the second only city in India (besides <a href="/wiki/Kolkata" title="Kolkata">Kolkata</a>) to have a functional tram transport. In 2017, the local MLA <a href="/wiki/Shrikant_Sharma" title="Shrikant Sharma">Shrikant Sharma</a> announced that the trams will be operational in Mathura and <a href="/wiki/Vrindavan" title="Vrindavan">Vrindavan</a> by 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air">Air</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mathura&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Air">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Currently the city has no airport. The nearest airports are the <a href="/wiki/Agra_Airport" title="Agra Airport">Agra Airport</a> (about 60&#160;km away) and the <a href="/wiki/Indira_Gandhi_International_Airport" title="Indira Gandhi International Airport">Delhi Airport</a> (about 160&#160;km away) with major national and international air routes.The under-construction <a href="/wiki/Jewar_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewar Airport">Jewar Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Greater_Noida" title="Greater Noida">Greater Noida</a> is approximately 75&#160;km from Mathura and is expected to be country's largest airport when fully operational. Land has been earmarked, and construction is in progress near the <a href="/wiki/Yamuna_Expressway" title="Yamuna Expressway">Yamuna Expressway</a>, with plans to open in the next five years with regular flights to major national and international air routes in future.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2012, the then civil aviation minister <a href="/wiki/Ajit_Singh_(Indian_politician)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ajit Singh (Indian politician)">Ajit Singh</a> suggested Mathura's name for the site of a new greenfield international airport to the then chief minister of <a href="/wiki/Uttar_Pradesh" title="Uttar Pradesh">Uttar Pradesh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Akhilesh_Yadav" title="Akhilesh Yadav">Akhilesh Yadav</a>. Mathura's name came to note when a group of ministers terminated the plan of building <a href="/wiki/Taj_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Taj International Airport">Taj International Airport</a> at Agra.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Strategic_importance">Strategic importance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mathura&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Strategic importance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/I_Corps_(India)" title="I Corps (India)">I Corps</a> (Strike Formation)<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> within the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Army" title="Indian Army">Indian Army</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Central_Command_(India)" title="Central Command (India)">Central Command</a> is based in Mathura, hosting Strike I Corps headquarters in a large classified area in the outskirts of the city known as Mathura Cantonment (Central Command is headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Lucknow" title="Lucknow">Lucknow</a>). It hosts Strike Infantry units, air defence units, armoured divisions, engineer brigades, artillery Units, and classified units of <a href="/wiki/Strategic_Forces_Command" title="Strategic Forces Command">Strategic Forces Command</a>. The I Corps is primarily responsible for the western borders of India. In 2007 during Exercise Ashwamedha, all the armoured, artillery, and infantry divisions performed a simulation of an overall NBC (nuclear-chemical-biological) environment. The aim was to show operational ability in high intensity, short duration and 'sudden' battle<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Industries">Industries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mathura&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Industries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Mathura_Refinery" title="Mathura Refinery">Mathura Refinery</a> located in the city is one of the biggest oil refineries of Asia with a refining capacity of 8.0&#160;million <a href="/wiki/Tonne" title="Tonne">tonnes</a> per year.<sup id="cite_ref-Iocl.com_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Iocl.com-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> This oil refinery of <a href="/wiki/Indian_Oil_Corporation" title="Indian Oil Corporation">Indian Oil Corporation</a> Ltd. is a technologically advanced oil refinery and provides local employment opportunities as well. Its main focus is to meet the  demands from the <a href="/wiki/National_Capital_Region_(India)" title="National Capital Region (India)">NCR</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Iocl.com_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Iocl.com-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> The refinery had undertaken projects to upgrade its diesel and gasoline units to bring Sulphur levels down by nearly 80 percent<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_and_communications">Media and communications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mathura&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Media and communications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The city has a local station of the <a href="/wiki/All_India_Radio" title="All India Radio">All India Radio</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Educational_institutions">Educational institutions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mathura&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Educational institutions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<li><a href="/wiki/U.P._Pt._Deen_Dayal_Upadhyaya_Veterinary_Science_University_and_Cattle_Research_Institute" title="U.P. Pt. Deen Dayal Upadhyaya Veterinary Science University and Cattle Research Institute">U.P. Pt. Deen Dayal Upadhyaya Veterinary Science University and Cattle Research Institute</a><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
